دليل آخر وهو الوجه الثالث من الوجوه الدالة على زيادة الوجود في الواجب الوجوب الذاتي إضافة تقتضي في الواجب طرفين أحدهما الماهية والآخر الوجود لأنه عبارة عن اقتضاء الماهية للوجود فيكون وجوده زائداً على ماهيته قلنا كون الوجوب إضافة ممنوع بل هو نفس الماهية لأن الوجوب هو الأمر الذي به يمتاز ذلك الواجب عن غيره وذلك الأمر هو ذات الواجب لأنه بذاته ممتاز عن غيره والصواب أن يقال : إن القوة . قوله : ( وهو الوجه الثالث إلخ ) غير الأسلوب إشارة إلى أنه ليس بمثابة تلك الوجوه في القوة . قوله : (والصواب إلخ) يعني أن الجواب بإنكار كون الوجوب إضافة خطأ، فإن مقابلته لازم على المصنف إذ لا يلزم هذا القول منه بل الظاهر من كلامه أن الوجود عين الماهية حيث قال : وإن سلمنا أن الوجود أمر مشترك معنى فإنه يدل على منع اشتراك الوجود معنى، وليس ذلك إلا عند الأشعري القائل بأن الوجود عين الماهية وليس في كلامه تصريح بأن هذا الاعتراض من جانب الحكيم، حتى يلزم عدم صحة القول باتحاد الوجود الخاص والماهية في الممكنات لأن قوله : وإن سلمنا إلخ لا يناسب مذهب الحكيم كما تحققت نعم قوله : في تقرير الاعتراض الأول فالأشياء التي يصدق عليها أنه وجود لا موجود يدل على أن الوجود الخاص مغاير للماهية فيلزم منه ثلاثة أشياء . قوله : ( لأنه عبارة عن اقتضاء الماهية للوجود قيل : الواجب بمعنى ما يقتضي ذاته وجوده ليس بمتحقق عند الحكماء، وإنما المتحقق عندهم هو الواجب بمعنى المستغني عن الغير وقسمة الموجود إلى الواجب بالمعنى الأول، وإلى الممكن تقسيم له بحسب الاحتمال العقلي لا أن كلا قسميه موجودان في الخارج، وقد صرح بذلك الشيخ في إلهيات الشفاء، حيث قال إن الأمور التي تدخل في الوجود تحتمل في العقل الانقسام إلى قسمين فيكون منها ما إذا اعتبر بذاته لم يجب وجوده فظاهر أنه لا يمتنع له أيضاً وجوده ، وإلا لم يدخل في الوجود وهذا الشيء حيز الإمكان، ويكون منها ما إذا اعتبر بذاته وجب وجوده، وأقول قال الشيخ في مفتتح رسالة ألفها في بيان كيفية زيارة القبور وجدواها اعلم أن لهذه المسألة مقدمات فينبغي أن تعرف أولاً حتى تستنتج منها المطالب وهي معرفة الموجودات الآخذة من المبدأ الأول وهو العلة الأولى المسماة عند الحكماء بواجب الوجود، وأعني بواجب الوجود أن يكون وجوده من غيره هذا كلامه، وهو صريح في القول بأن واجب الوجود عز وجل يقتضي ذاته وجوده، وأما ما ذكره في إلهيات الشفاء فلا يدل على خلاف هذا، إذ ليس مراده هناك إلا أن حصر الموجود في القسمين حصر عقلي أي لا ثالث لهما عنده ولو بطريق الاستدلال، وأن الشيء الأول هو الممكن لا أن أحد القسمين محتمل صرف لا وجود له في الخارج. قوله : (والصواب أن يقال : إلخ) سيجيء أن الوجوب يطلق على ثلاثة معان ذاته لا من هي استغناؤه
Another proof, which is the third aspect among the aspects indicating the addition of existence in the Necessary: Essential necessity is a relation that requires in the Necessary two sides: one is the essence and the other is existence, because it is an expression of the essence's requiring existence; thus its existence is additional to its essence. We said: The claim that necessity is a relation is denied; rather it is the essence itself, because necessity is that by which the Necessary is distinguished from others, and that thing is the essence of the Necessary because it is distinguished from others by its essence. The correct thing is to say: that the strength. (His saying: 'And it is the third aspect etc.') He changed the style to indicate that it is not on the level of those aspects in strength. (His saying: 'And the correct thing etc.') means that the answer by denying that necessity is a relation is wrong, for its confrontation is binding upon the author, since this saying does not follow from him; rather the apparent meaning of his words is that existence is identical to essence, where he said: 'And if we grant that existence is a common meaning' – for it indicates the denial of existence being a common meaning, and that is only according to the Ash'ari who says that existence is identical to essence; and in his words there is no explicit statement that this objection is from the side of the philosopher (al-hakim), so that the falsehood of the saying about the union of particular existence and essence in contingents is not necessitated, because his saying 'And if we grant etc.' does not suit the philosopher's school as you have verified. Yes, his saying in the formulation of the first objection: 'The things of which it is predicated that they are existence, not existent' indicates that particular existence is other than essence, and thus three things follow from it. (His saying: 'Because it is an expression of the essence's requiring existence.') It was said: The Necessary in the sense of that whose essence requires its existence is not realized among the philosophers; rather what is realized among them is the Necessary in the sense of being independent of others; and the division of the existent into the Necessary in the first sense and the contingent is a division according to rational possibility, not that both of its two parts exist in the external world. The Master (al-Shaykh) has stated this in the Metaphysics (Ilahiyyat) of the Healing (al-Shifa'), where he said: 'The things that enter into existence admit in the intellect division into two parts: among them is that which, if considered in itself, its existence is not necessary, so it is clear that its existence is also not impossible, otherwise it would not enter into existence, and this thing is the domain of possibility; and among them is that which, if considered in itself, its existence is necessary.' And I say: The Master said in the opening of a treatise he wrote on the manner of visiting graves and its benefit: 'Know that this issue has premises that should be known first so that the conclusions may be derived from them; they are the knowledge of existing things taking from the First Principle, which is the First Cause, called by the philosophers the Necessary Existence (wajib al-wujud). And by Necessary Existence I mean that its existence is from other than itself.' This is his speech, and it is explicit in saying that the Necessary Existence, may He be exalted, His essence requires His existence. As for what he mentioned in the Metaphysics of the Healing, it does not indicate contrary to this, for his intention there is only that the restriction of the existent to two parts is an intellectual restriction, i.e., there is no third for him, even if by way of deduction, and that the first thing is the contingent, not that one of the two parts is a pure potentiality with no existence in the external world. (His saying: 'And the correct thing is to say etc.') It will come that necessity (wujub) is applied to three meanings: its essence... not from... it is its independence.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents a third proof that existence is additional to the Necessary Being's essence, based on the concept of necessity (wujub). The argument states: necessity is a relation (idafa) that requires two sides: the essence and existence, because necessity is the essence's requiring existence; hence existence is additional. The response denies that necessity is a relation; rather, it is the essence itself, because necessity is what distinguishes the Necessary from others, and that is its essence. The commentary explains that this answer (denying necessity as a relation) is incorrect, because the author's own words (in the previous objection) suggest existence is identical to essence (according to Ash'ari), but the opponent (philosopher) might not agree. It then delves into a discussion about the meaning of 'wajib al-wujud' among philosophers. It cites Ibn Sina's Metaphysics: the division into necessary and contingent is a rational division, not necessarily that both kinds exist externally. A quote from a treatise by Ibn Sina seems at odds, but the commentator reconciles it: Ibn Sina's definition 'existence from other than itself' applies to the contingent, not to the Necessary. The passage concludes by noting that the term 'wujub' has three meanings, which will come later. The final cut-off line likely refers to the essence, not something else, and that independence is one meaning.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the proof from necessity (wujub) as a relation is decisive and shows existence must be added.
Correction: The proof is weak; necessity can be identified with the essence itself, so no addition is required. The rebuttal denying necessity as a relation is also not the final answer; the correct understanding involves distinguishing different meanings of necessity and analyzing the philosophical context.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the initial rebuttal to the argument that necessity (wujub) is a relation?
A) Necessity is a relation that requires only one side.
B) Necessity is identical to the essence of the Necessary, not an added relation.
C) Necessity is not a real attribute but a mental concept.
D) The argument is sound but applies only to contingents.

Key Takeaway
The argument that necessity is a relation fails because necessity is identical to the essence of the Necessary Being; any addition of existence is not required.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage argues that necessity is not a relation added to God's essence but is His very essence. Do you sometimes treat your awareness of Allah's necessity as a mere intellectual addition to your faith, rather than the core that defines your entire existence before Him? What would it mean for you to live as if His necessity were your essence, not just a belief?
?
Ibn Sina defines the Necessary Being as 'independent from others' (المستغني عن الغير). In what areas of your life do you still depend on created things as if they were necessary, forgetting that only Allah is truly self-sufficient? How can you shift your heart's reliance from these to Him alone?
?
The proof from necessity is presented as weak and rebutted. Are there arguments for God's existence that you hold onto as decisive, yet deep down you know your faith relies on more than intellectual proof? If the 'third proof' were to collapse, would your certainty in Allah remain? Why or why not?
